ARIE 1922-1923 [vol. 045]


A.--List of copper-plates examined during the year 1922-23.


ARIE/1922-1923/A/1922-23/1 (page 10)

Government Epigraphist for India.

Origin

Edition
…
Remarks
Damaged and sense obscure. Seems to record a gift of land and money by one Vaḍa Nāyar of Pūdavāḍi for worship and offerings in the temple of Tirunelli-Āḷvāṉ. The land and money were left in charge of different indivi-duals for the supply of the necessary rice, oil, fruits, etc.
ARIE/1922-1923/A/1922-23/2 (page 10)
Placement
Do.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Makara of the year with Jupiter in Kaṟkaṭaka.
Language
Tamil in Vaṭṭeḻuttu
Origin
Returned to the Government Epigraphist for India.
Edition
…
Remarks
Records a gift of 35 kaḻañju of gold for burn-ing a perpetual lamp in the temple of Dēva-dēvēśaṉ Tiruvaḍi at Tirunelli by a certain Kōdai Ïrāmanāya... of Vaḷḷuva-nāḍu. The dēvakarmis of Nelkkuṉṟam, including the Paṇḍāravāriyar, received the gold and undertook to provide for the burning of the lamp by commuting its interest in paddy into that of oil from the residents of Iḷam-bilāchchēri.

ARIE/1922-1923/A/1922-23/5 (page 10)
Placement
Mr. Rm.St.Sivanandam Pillai, Kumbhakonām, through Mr.P.V.Jagadisa Ayyar.
Dynasty
Pallava
King
Kō-Vijaya-Nandivikrama-varman.
Date
61st year
Language
Grantha & Tamil
Origin
Returned to the Government Epigraphist for India.
Edition
…
Remarks
Gift of 16 vēli of land free of taxes in Nalgūr newly constituted into a brahmadēya village called Paṭṭattāḷmaṅgalam to a number of Brāhmaṇas at the request of Maṅgala-nāḍāḷvāṉ. This included the 12 vēli of land already granted as brahmadēya in the 59th year of the king. The ājñapti was Vijaya-nallūḻāṉ of Ālappākkam. The engraver of these plates was Śrī Daṇḍi, son of Viḍēlvi-ḍugu Pallavapperundachchaṉ of Aimbaṉiach-chēri of Kachchippēḍu.
ARIE/1922-1923/A/1922-23/6 (page 11)
Placement
Mr. M.N.Srinivasacharya, the late Panditi of this office.
Dynasty
Vijayanagara
King
Veṅkaṭapatirāya-Mahārāya
Date
Śaka 1513, Khara, Āshā-ḍha, śu., paurṇimā, Lunar ec-lipse.
Language
Sanskrit (Nandināgarī)
Origin
Under corre-spondence.
Edition
…
Remarks
Records the gift by the king, of the village Kāyāru with its hamlet (upagrāma) called Vaḍakkuppaṭṭu, situated in Raṇḍāyiram-vēlipaṭṭu in Kumuḷi-nāḍu a sub-division of Āmūru-kōṭṭam in Paḍavīḍu-mahārājya and in Chaṅgaḷanīrpaṭṭu-sīmā, as sarvamānya to learned Brāhmaṇas, divided into 84 shares and surnamed Chañchasamudra. The grant was made at the request (vijñapti) of the geṇeral (sēnēśa) Cheṁchabhūpa who was the son of the chief (bhūpāla) Ahōbalēśa and the Governor of Chandragiri and other forts. Among the donees were many scholars learned in grammar (śabda-śāstra) and astronomy (jyōtisha).
ARIE/1922-1923/A/1922-23/7 (page 11)
Placement
Do.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Veṅkaṭapatirāya
Date
Saka 1534, Parīdhāvi, Māgha, śu. saptamī.
Language
Sanskrit, (Nandinagari)
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
…
Remarks
Records the gift of the village Muruga-maṅgalam surnamed Gōpālaśrīsamudra situated in the Paḍavīḍu-mahārājya, Toṇḍīra-maṇḍala, Cheṅgalippaṭṭu-sīmā, Raṇḍāyirapaṭṭu, Kumuḷi-nāḍu and Āmūri-kōṭṭa as sarvamānya to the scholar, Rāma-kṛishṇa-jōsya of the Harita-gōtra, Āpas-tamba-sūtra, and Yajuś-śākhā who was well versed in the Vēdas, Vēdāṅgas, Tarka (logic), Smṛiti and Sūryasiddhanta, and who was the son of Mallikārjunārādhya and Gaṅgāmbikā and the grandson of Liṅganārādhya of the Svaramaṇḍala family. The grant was made in the presence of the god Veṅkaṭēśa.

Remarks
Records the grant by Triṇayana-Pallava of the village Lavaṇapura (Uppuṭūru) to several Erāhmaṇas of the Yājñavalkya seet whose names and respective shares are enumerated. This grant seems to have been engraved during the time of the Vijaya-nagara king Vijaya-Bhūpati.
ARIE/1922-1923/A/1922-23/9 (page 11)
Placement
The late Mr. K.V.Laksh-mana Rao, M.A., Telugu Encyclopaedia Office, Egmere.
Dynasty
Reḍḍi
King
Anna-Vēma (entitled) Vīra-Nārāyaṇa.
Date
Śaka 1293, Rādhā (i.e., Vaiśākha), Lunar eclipse.
Language
Sanskrit (in Telugu) & Telugu
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
…
Remarks
States that the king succeeded his brother An-na-Pōta to his ancestral throne. Records the re-grant to several brahmans of the village Uppugallu which had been resumed some time previously. The names and gōtras of the donees with their respective shares are enumerated. The inscription was composed by Bālasarasvatī.

Begins with a salutation to Mukhyaprāṇa (i.e., Hanumān). Records a settlement regarding the villages in which the taḷavārike (i.e., police) rights respectively of the taḷavāras of Kuḍatane and Bhāṇarāvi were fixed in the presence of a pañchāyati.

Remarks
Records the grant of the village Nīlambēru clubbed with the village Puttūru, both to-gether renamed as Achyutēndrasamudra by Bālabhūpati, son of Chennarāja of the Solar race and Kāśyapa-gōtra by order of the king. Bālabhūpati is stated to have been govern-ing the Koṅgu-rājya with his capital at Rājarājanagara.
ARIE/1922-1923/A/1922-23/14 (page 12)

Remarks
Records the grant of a field in the village of Iṟbuli in Karmarāshṭra by Pṛithvī Duvarāja in the presence of Vallabha to brahman called Vēda-Śarman, a resident of Mugamūr, belonging to the Śaṇḍilyāyana-gōtra and Āpastamba-sūtra. The boundaries of the land granted are also given.
ARIE/1922-1923/A/1922-23/15 (page 12)
Placement
The Collector of Kistna
Dynasty
Reḍḍi
King
Anna-Vēma
Date
Śaka 1293, Pausha, ba. 5, Saturday, Makara-(Saṁkra-mana).
Language
Sanskrit & Telugu in Telugu
Origin
Purchased for the Government Museum, Madras.
Edition
…
Remarks
Records the gift of the village Drujjavaram surnamed as Annavēmapura on the banks of the river Malāpahā in the Kurttidēśa by the king, to the brahman Appayārya who was the purōhita of the king and to his three younger brothers Śrīrāma-Bhaṭṭa, Pinnaya-Bhaṭṭa, and Sūri-Bhaṭṭa. These were the sons of Allāḍa-Bhaṭṭa and belonged to the Śrīvatsa-gōtra. Pinnaya-Bhaṭṭa is said to have been the king's adviser on Dharma (i.e., law).

ARIE/1922-1923/B/1922/313 (page 14)

On a slab set up in a field to the east of Tamballapalle.

Language
Telugu & Kannaḍa
Remarks
Registers the confirmation by the king of the grant of the village Tammaḍiyarahaḷḷi and of the gift (kāṇike) money realized on the days of Śivarātri, to the temple of Malli-kārjuna at Chandragiri, previously made by Kampaṇṇa-Oḍeya and Chikka-Oḍeya. Regulates the shares to be enjoyed by the several priests of the temple. The king is stated to have been ruling at Penugoṇḍa-paṭṭaṇa.

Mentions the taxes vishaya-suṅka and birāḍāya and the village Veḷuṅguguṇṭa (modern Veligallu).

Remarks
States that a certain Timmarāja, son of Hiriya Abbarāja of Harige, belonging to the Kāśyapa-gōtra and Apastamba-sūtra, installed the image of the god Raghunāthadēva at the Penugoṇḍa gate to the east of Varadājiyammana-paṭṭaṇa and made grants of some lands to the god. This is a copy of A.R. No. 16 of 1889 (No. 245 of South-Indian Inscriptions, Vol. IV.)

ARIE/1922-1923/B/1922/779 (page 56)
Placement
On the Nandi-pillar planted before the Amarēśvara temple in the same village.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Kali 2000 (?) Ardhō-daya.
Language
Sanskrit (prose & verse) in Telugu & Telugu
Remarks
Purports to record the grant of the village Lavanapura (Uppuṭūru) to 1,000 brahmans who were the followers of Yājñavalkya and who are said to have come from the town Ahichchhatrapura on the banks of the Ganges, by Trinētra-Pallava. Also records the measurements of the streets called Sōmavīdhi and Sūryavīdhi as well as the house-sites that were presented and the garden and the arable lands allotted to each share. It also records certain agreements made between the shareholders as to selling shares in the village to outsiders and receiving dowries for girls in marriage. Separate shares were allotted to the gods Mahādēva, Kēśava and Vighnēśvara and to the god-dess Pādāmbikāśaktī. The extent of the village and its boundaries are given at great length and with minute details. See C.P.No. 8 of Appendix A above.

Mentions also Achalapura, the Vallabha and the Chōḷa kings. Refers to the burning of Kiraṇapura and the conquest of Saṅkila. See Ibid. No. 39.

ARIE/1922-1923/B/1922/841 (page 62)
Placement
On a slab planted opposite to the Sītārāmasvāmin temple in the same village.
Dynasty
Gōlkoṇḍa
King
Mahamandu Pādaśahā, ruling from the Aśvapati throne at Gōlakoṇḍa.
Date
Śaka 1522, Śārvari, Nija-Śrāvaṇa, śu. 7, Wednesday 'Suhṛisan (i.e., Sūr-san or Shahūr San) Alaphunēku 1008, Ihari Alaphuchamdu... Safar, Sanati [sphā]alapu.’
Language
Telugu verse & prose
Remarks
Registers the conditions of settlement made by the king's general Ekalāsukhānu for the village Ekalāsukhānapēṭa founded by him near Dharmāvuram in the Addaṅki-sīma. Mentions the conquests of Rājamahēndram and Koṇḍavīḍu by his senior and junior commanders respectively. This inscription is not published in the Nellore Inscriptions.

Remarks
Begins with the introduction “pukazmAtu viLagka,” etc. Records an order of the great assembly of Rājēndraśōḻa-chaturvēdimaṅgalam (i.e. Uttiramērūr), an independent village in Kāliyūr-kōṭṭam, a subdivision of Jayaṅgoṇḍa-śōḻa-maṇḍalam, remitting the taxes on 30 pāḍagam of land purchased by Araiyaṉ Gaṅgaikoṇḍāṉār alias Śōḻa-vichchādarap-Pallavaraiyar of Iraiyūr in Pāṇḍikulāśaṉi-vaḷanāḍu, a subdivision of Śōḻa-maṇḍalam, and granted by him along with a house-site purchased with the money given by Tirumaḻiśai-Vaḷḷal and Vīṟṟirundāṉ-Dāsaṉ for the maintenance of a maṭha called Aruḷāḷadāsaṉ which he had founded. The land was lying fallow for 60 or 70 years and was now called Śōḻavichchādira-viḷāgam after the donor. The tax on the land was exempted for the current (46th) year, but for the years following five kāśu per annum was to be levied on the land. Other taxes such as piḍāgai-vari, uppu-kāśu etc., were remitted altogether.

Vīra-Pāṇḍyadēva
Date
25th year, 265th day.
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Records an order of Kulaśēkharach-Chambuvarāya exempt-ing the residents of the streets round the temple of Śokkapperumāḷ from the payment of taxes on looms and oil mills as in the case of those living round the temple of Tirukkēdāramuḍaiya-Nāyaṉār.
ARIE/1922-1923/C/1923/196 (page 80)
Placement
On the north wall of the kitchen in the same temple.
Dynasty
…
King
Vijaya-Gaṇḍagōpāladēva
Date
28th year Karka-ṭaka, śu. shashṭhī, [Sunday], Viśā-khā.
Language
Grantha & Tamil
Remarks
The king bears a number of birudas and calls himself a Pallava. Registers the grant of the southern hamlet of Kūḍalūr together with all its taxes as a tiruviḍaiyāṭṭam to the god Śokkapperumāḷ in the temple of Rājēndraśōḻa-Viṇṇa[gar-Emberumāṉ] at Uttaramēru alias Gaṇḍagō-pāla-chaturvēdimaṅgalam.
ARIE/1922-1923/C/1923/197 (page 80)
Placement
On a slab built into the south wall of the Hanumān shrine in front of the same temple.
Dynasty
Chōḷa
King
Rājarājakēsarivarman
Date
9th year, 158th day
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Incomplete. Seems to record the decision of the village assembly about the payment of fines imposed on the several castes and communities at Uttaramēlūr. Mentions the mukha-maṇḍapa of the Tulābhāra-Śrīkōyil where the assembly held its sittings.
ARIE/1922-1923/C/1923/198 (page 80)
Placement
On the north wall of the central shrine in the Vyāghrapurīśvara temple at Tiruppulivanam.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Tribhuvanachakravartin Kulōttuṅga-Chōḷadēva.
Date
12th year
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Records the royal grant, free of taxes, of 60 vēli of land at Pāppaṉṉallūr in Vētuṅgāḍu-nāḍu to the temple of Tiruppulivalamuḍaiya-Mahādēva at Rājēndraśōḻa-cha-turvēdimaṅgalam, a subdivision of Kāliyūr-kōṭṭam, a district of Jayaṅgoṇḍaśōḻa-maṇḍalam on the representa-tion of Mīṉavaṉ-Mūvēndavēḷāṉ. The king was seated under the canopy of pearls on his throne in the corona-tion hall of his palace at Vikramaśōḻapuram while issuing the order.
ARIE/1922-1923/C/1923/199 (page 80)
Placement
On the same wall

Built in in the middle. Seems to record a sale of the village Araśāṇipālai by a certain Pāmbaṇindāṉ, a native of Śēṟṟūr in Uyyakoṇḍārśōḻa-vaḷanāḍu, to whom it had been sold some time previously owing to hard times.

Dynasty

King
Sakalalōkachakravartin Rājanārāyaṇa Śambuvarāya.
Date
7th year, Tulā, śu. shashṭhī, Mon-day.
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Built in in the middle. Seems to record the amicable settlement of some dispute between the residents of two villages regarding the flow of water from the tank at Tiruppulivaṉam and the grant of land as tirunāmattuk-kāṇi to the temple of the god Tiruppulivaṉamuḍaiya-Nāya[ṉār].
ARIE/1922-1923/C/1923/201 (page 81)
Placement
On the west wall of the same shrine
Dynasty
Vijayanagara
King
Vīra Viruppaṇa-Uḍaiyar
Date
Vipa (Vibhava ?), Mārgaḻi, 12.
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Records the assurance, given to the weavers of Tiruppuli-vaṉam who had deserted the village owing to their inability to pay taxes, that except a consolidated amount of 5 paṇam on every loom per year, no other tax would be collected from them in future.
ARIE/1922-1923/C/1923/202 (page 81)
Placement
On the south and east walls of the Dakshiṇāmūrti shrine adjoining the same shrine.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Vīrapratāpa Dēvarāya-Mahārāya
Date
Śaka 1356, Ānanda, Mēsha, śu. ashṭa-mī, Friday, Pūśam (Pushya).
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Gift of the hamlet of Karuvēppampūṇḍi by the assembly of Uttaramēru alias Rājēndraśōḻa-chaturvēdimaṅgalam as a tirunāmattukkāṇi to the temple of Tiruppulivaṉam-uḍaiya-Nāyaṉār. Refers to a similar previous gift of Tiruchchitrakūḍanallūr made to the temple by the same assembly in the year Vibha[va*], Ṛishabha, śu. daśamī, Uttiram, Sunday.
ARIE/1922-1923/C/1923/203 (page 81)
Placement
On the south wall of the maṇḍapa in front of the central shrine.

King
Do. do.
Date
5th year, Mīna, śu. tṛitīyā, Rēvatī, Tuesday.
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Gift of 115 cows for the daily supply of milk for the sacred bath and offerings of the god by certain shepherds on behalf of Viradamuḍittāṉ Bagavatiyāḷvāṉ Śēdirāyadēvar who had rescued the cows and sheep belonging to these shepherds which had been plundered by certain persons.

15th year
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Records the grant of the privilege of waving the chāmara in front of the image during the car processions, to a dancing girl of the temple, named Piraināṟuśīraḍiyār and to her descendents in recognition of her gift of a golden necklace to the god in the 8th year of the king and of a silver plate and a four-sided procession car to the temple in the 15th year.

King
Vīrapratāpa Dēvarāya-Mahārāya
Date
Śaka 1348, Viśvā-vasu, Kanyā, śu. pañchamī, Wed-nesday. Uttiram.
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Registers an order of Salakkaya-Nāyakkar, the agent of mahāpradhāni Mallarasa-Uḍaiyar to the weavers and other craftemen of Tiruppulivaṉam in Pulivaṉa-nāḍu which was a tirunāmattukkāṇi of the temple, fixing the total amount of the taxes on the several professions to be paid annually to the temple.
ARIE/1922-1923/C/1923/215 (page 82)
